The college is divided into ten divisions or academic units. All major ADA-recognized dental specialties are represented. The College has approximately 600 students in its undergraduate and graduate programs.  <br> <br>   \r\n\r\nThe Ohio State University College of Dentistry is seeking a Dental Assistant for its affiliated Dental Faculty Practice (DFP). When our faculty is not teaching the next generation of dentists, our faculty dentists provide expert care for children and adults through DFP and provide virtually every area of dental care available in one location. <br> <br> \r\n\r\nThis position provides instrument sterilization to the Dental Faculty Practice of 50+ dentists and hygienists to maintain efficient workflow for the practice; provides support to the dental hygienists and provides clinical dental assisting to the orthodontists in the Dental Faculty Practice; performs autoclave maintenance and monitoring, maintain stockroom and waste-management, sterilize instruments, and assist dental hygienists with charting, transcribing, patient flow, room preparation, radiographs, and additional support to temporary dental hygienists, assists with overflow and additional rooms for dental hygienists; provides clinical and laboratory support to the orthodontists; provides indirect assistance in patient treatment including but not limit to: charting, room preparation, scheduling patients, contacting patients by email and phone; provides direct assistance in patient treatment including but not limited to: taking records, scanning, taking impressions, exposing radiographs, removing wires and auxiliaries, and remove elastics.<br> <br>     \r\n\r\nThis position requires successful completion of drug & alcohol screening.    A dental assistant needs to be able to: use of both hands, dexterity in the fingers and the ability to manipulate instruments, materials, dental hand pieces, and operate dental equipment. The body must be able to reach, bend, stoop and reach in or order to perform most dental assistant jobs. The use of feet is necessary to manipulate the rheostat for hand pieces or other dental equipment. The body must be able to work from a dental stool in order to perform most dental procedures. The ability to sit and stand for a duration of time is also necessary. Other specific requirements include color spectrum differentiation; manual dexterity/motor coordination, hand-eye coordination, physical communications; visual acuity and communication/language development. We are seeking candidates with demonstrated interest in developing and managing an interdisciplinary, extramurally funded, and internationally-recognized integrated research program applying population genetics, statistical genetics, genomics, and bioinformatics to the development and improvement of crops for sustainable biomaterials, especially biopolymers. The position has research, teaching, and service responsibilities. The candidate will teach a course in their area of expertise, which may include principles of population genetics, methods associated with analyses of genome-wide data, genetic improvement of outcrossing species, and plant domestication. Participation as guest lecturer in team-taught courses is expected, in addition to facilitating graduate-level journal-club, seminars, and methods classes as needed. <br> <br>\r\n\r\nThis will be a full time, 9 month, tenure-track appointment to begin fall semester 2015. The salary and teaching load are competitive with other major research institutions. The position is open at the Assistant Professor level, although we prefer candidates with some experience and a record of scholarly research. <br> <br> \r\n\r\nThis position is partially funded by Ohio State’s Discovery Themes Initiative, a significant faculty hiring investment in key thematic areas in which the university can build on its culture of academic collaboration to make a global impact. The successful candidate will be joining a highly collaborative interdisciplinary community of scholars in the Sustainable and Resilient Economy (S&RE) program, which takes a holistic approach to understanding how production and consumption systems are linked to ecological systems, and how society can achieve more sustainable and resilient development. This program aims to stimulate innovations that enhance the value and reduce the adverse impacts of material flows through the economy and society, and will provide a rigorous evaluation of the costs, benefits, and potential hidden consequences of changes in technology, policy, and the natural environment. <br> <br>\r\n\r\nCommitment to Diversity and Inclusion: The Ohio State University is committed to establishing a culturally and intellectually diverse environment, encouraging all members of our learning community to reach their full potential. We are seeking candidates with demonstrated interest in developing and managing an interdisciplinary, extramurally funded, and internationally-recognized integrated research program applying population genetics, statistical genetics, genomics, and bioinformatics to the development and improvement of crops for sustainable biomaterials, especially biopolymers. The position has research, teaching, and service responsibilities. The candidate will teach a course in their area of expertise, which may include principles of population genetics, methods associated with analyses of genome-wide data, genetic improvement of outcrossing species, and plant domestication. Participation as guest lecturer in team-taught courses is expected, in addition to facilitating graduate-level journal-club, seminars, and methods classes as needed. <br> <br>\r\n\r\nThis will be a full time, 9 month, tenure-track appointment to begin fall semester 2015. The successful candidate will be joining a highly collaborative interdisciplinary community of scholars in the Sustainable and Resilient Economy (S&RE) program, which takes a holistic approach to understanding how production and consumption systems are linked to ecological systems, and how society can achieve more sustainable and resilient development. This program aims to stimulate innovations that enhance the value and reduce the adverse impacts of material flows through the economy and society, and will provide a rigorous evaluation of the costs, benefits, and potential hidden consequences of changes in technology, policy, and the natural environment. <br> <br>\r\n\r\nCommitment to Diversity and Inclusion: The Ohio State University is committed to establishing a culturally and intellectually diverse environment, encouraging all members of our learning community to reach their full potential. The principal gifts team works with these key partners to translate and shape big, fundable ideas into transformational gift opportunities. \r\n<br><br>\r\nThe efforts of the Principal gifts team ultimately drive the creation of informed, long-range strategies for prospects-honoring their passions and respecting their multiple interests, bridging external interests with institutional need, and allowing our donors to stretch their philanthropic partnership with the Ohio State University. <br><br>\r\n<b>Position Overview</b><br>\r\nThe Senior Director of Development reports to the Vice President for Principal Gifts and supports Ohio state university by marrying big multi-disciplinary ideas with the passionate interests of our prospects. The Office of Investments was created to ensure strategic management of The University's Long-Term Investment Pool and its goal is to deliver long-term, attractive, risk-adjusted returns to support the educational and research goals of the university. The investment team continuously strives to identify market opportunities where price and underlying value are misaligned.   <br> <br>\r\n\r\nAs an integral part of the Investment Office working under the direction of the Director of Liquid Strategies, this position will contribute to the decision making of the $3.5 billion asset pool through active research of macro and micro factors, as well as, support decision making through leading the monitoring and evaluation process for absolute return and directional liquid managers and strategies in the fixed income allocation.  This position provides experience in investment management analysis and modeling. <br> <br> \r\n\r\n\r\n<b> Position Overview: </b> \r\nWorking among a collaborative, close knit, high-performing team, the ideal candidate must have the ability to sort through large amounts of information and determine what is pertinent and what is routine in order to provide the critical support that maximizes the performance of the endowment portfolio.  He/she should also possess a natural curiosity regarding economic and financial markets to conduct research on the macro environment focusing on the global economic, equity and credit environments.  Responsibilities also include underwriting liquid global credit investment vehicles, participating in the due diligence process including completing market research, evaluating historic investment performances, performing reference checking and overseeing investment manager relationships.  He/she will evaluate, develop and use analytical tools to aid in the investment process for liquid global credit managers and articulate complex financial concepts both verbally and in written form.  <br> <br>\r\n\r\n\r\n<b> Position Objectives:</b> \r\n<ul> <li> Become familiar with current managers in the liquid fixed income allocation through conference calls, meetings and consultant reports.\r\n<li> Establish a process for monitoring and updating macro variables (economic and financial market related) for monthly investment team meetings and for presentations to University affiliated entities.\r\n<li> Become proficient in using Code Red and eVestment software.\r\n<li> Improve and enhance monthly reporting for the liquid fixed income  allocation.\r\n<li> Begin the process of reviewing prospective managers already in Code Red. \r\n<li> Continue the process of seeking new prospective managers.\r\n<li> Become familiar with current managers in the Global Equity allocation and provide investment perspective on hiring and monitoring.","summary":null,"date":"2015-03-23T13:30:10.000Z","pubdate":"2015-03-23T13:30:10.000Z","pubDate":"2015-03-23T13:30:10.000Z","link":"http://www.jobsatosu.com/postings/61745","guid":"61745","author":"Chief Investment Officer","comments":null,"origlink":null,"image":{},"source":{},"categories":[],"enclosures":[],"atom:@":{},"atom:id":{"@":{},"#":"61745"},"atom:published":{"@":{},"#":"2015-03-23T09:30:10-04:00"},"atom:updated":{"@":{},"#":"2015-03-23T09:30:10-04:00"},"atom:link":{"@":{"rel":"alternate","type":"text/html","href":"http://www.jobsatosu.com/postings/61745"}},"atom:title":{"@":{},"#":"Senior Investment Analyst"},"atom:content":{"@":{},"#":"<b> The Organization and The Opportunity: </b> \r\nThe Ohio State University, one of the nation’s leading public universities, is seeking applicants for the position of Senior Investment Analyst, in the Office of Investments. Responsibilities also include underwriting liquid global credit investment vehicles, participating in the due diligence process including completing market research, evaluating historic investment performances, performing reference checking and overseeing investment manager relationships.  He/she will evaluate, develop and use analytical tools to aid in the investment process for liquid global credit managers and articulate complex financial concepts both verbally and in written form.  <br> <br>\r\n\r\n\r\n<b> Position Objectives:</b> \r\n<ul> <li> Become familiar with current managers in the liquid fixed income allocation through conference calls, meetings and consultant reports.\r\n<li> Establish a process for monitoring and updating macro variables (economic and financial market related) for monthly investment team meetings and for presentations to University affiliated entities.\r\n<li> Become proficient in using Code Red and eVestment software.\r\n<li> Improve and enhance monthly reporting for the liquid fixed income  allocation.\r\n<li> Begin the process of reviewing prospective managers already in Code Red. \r\n<li> Continue the process of seeking new prospective managers.\r\n<li> Become familiar with current managers in the Global Equity allocation and provide investment perspective on hiring and monitoring."},"atom:author":{"@":{},"name":{"@":{},"#":"Chief Investment Officer"}},"meta":{"#ns":[{"xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2005/Atom"}],"@":[{"xml:lang":"en-US"},{"xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2005/Atom"}],"#xml":{"version":"1.0","encoding":"UTF-8"},"#content-type":{"#":"application/atom+xml; The Assistant Dean will play a key role in the development and implementation of admissions and financial aid strategy and will work in a collaborative manner with the offices of advancement, student affairs, communications, and career services.  <br> <br> \r\n    \r\nThis position is located on the main campus of The Ohio State University, one of the nation’s leading land grant research universities.  It is located in Columbus, Ohio approximately three miles north of the state capital.  The Moritz College of Law is consistently ranked among the top 20 public law schools in the nation and is Ohio’s top ranked law school.   Our core values are:  Excellence and Innovation, Integrity and Professionalism, Community and Individuality, Diversity and Inclusiveness.  <br> \r\n\r\nThe Ohio State University Moritz College of Law is actively committed to building and supporting a diverse community.  The University embraces human diversity and is committed to equal employment opportunity, valuing diversity in admissions, and eliminating discrimination.  This commitment is both a moral imperative consistent with an intellectual community that celebrates individual differences and diversity, as well as a matter of law.  Discrimination against any individual based upon protected status, which is defined as age, ancestry, color, disability, gender identity or expression, genetic information, HIV/AIDS status, military status, national origin, race, religion, sex, sexual orientation, or veteran status is prohibited.<br> <br> \r\n\r\nKey duties and responsibilities for the position are as follows:    \r\n<ul> <li> Develop and implement annual admissions criteria that govern the admissions process; Discrimination against any individual based upon protected status, which is defined as age, ancestry, color, disability, gender identity or expression, genetic information, HIV/AIDS status, military status, national origin, race, religion, sex, sexual orientation, or veteran status is prohibited.<br> <br> \r\n\r\nKey duties and responsibilities for the position are as follows:    \r\n<ul> <li> Develop and implement annual admissions criteria that govern the admissions process;  \r\n<li> Develop and lead the implementation of annual recruiting plans to take into account the college's enrollment goals and financial resources  \r\n<li> Represent the law school at  events aimed at attracting     prospective students\r\n<li> Supervise the Assistant Director for Financial Aid, the Assistant Director for Enrollment  Management and the Assistant Director for Admissions and Diversity Affairs  \r\n<li> Work closely and in a collaborative manner with the offices of advancement, student      affairs, communications and career services to promote the College's interest in recruiting and enrolling a talented and diverse group of students  \r\n<li> Develop metrics and assessment mechanisms for measuring and predicting progress toward attaining admissions goals throughout the recruiting season  \r\n<li> Provide annual reports to the faculty and to the National Council regarding admissions; \r\n<li> Promote and provide ethical and transparent communications with prospective students, law school constituencies and the general public \r\n<li> Ensure compliance with all ABA, LSAC, The Ohio State University and Moritz College of     Law policies, rules and regulations concerning recruiting and admission of incoming students  \r\n<li> Prepare annual reports to external evaluators\r\n<li> Work closely with the Associate Dean, faculty, staff and students to ensure an inclusive     environment that values all forms of diversity  \r\n<li> Meet on a regular and ongoing basis with the admissions staff to work with them on      achieving the College's enrollment and operational goals \r\n<li> Perform other related duties and tasks as assigned by the Dean.\r\n<li> The assistant dean reports to the associate dean.   \r\n<li> The position supervises a full-time staff of four."},"atom:author":{"@":{},"name":{"@":{},"#":"Law"}},"meta":{"#ns":[{"xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2005/Atom"}],"@":[{"xml:lang":"en-US"},{"xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2005/Atom"}],"#xml":{"version":"1.0","encoding":"UTF-8"},"#content-type":{"#":"application/atom+xml; ensures that all laboratories have an assigned qualified and trained instructor, that students are enrolled in the proper laboratory and that the laboratories operate according to departmental and national guidelines with respect to safety and pedagogy; develops and recommends new experiments and demonstrations; instructs and supervises laboratory teaching assistants in procedures, policies and teaching techniques; provides general supervision for all general chemistry courses (Chemistry 1110, 1210/1220, 16x0, and 19x0H); oversees daily operations and personnel in all day labs and night labs, including participating in and supervising the active walking of the labs, making teaching suggestions to teaching assistants, and answering student questions; directs the work of all laboratory teaching employees, including the direct supervision of the Assistant Lab Supervisor and the Evening Lab Lead; plans and oversees weekly mandatory staff meetings; revises all staff notes to include common mistakes by students and issues that arise in completing the lab as written; supervises the development of TA checklists for each experiment for quick reference.<br> <br> \r\n\r\nIn cooperation with the Undergraduate Program Director and the Vice Chair for Undergraduate Studies, determines and enforces standard laboratory policies, including both technical and safety issues; collaborates with the instructional staff to improve existing and develop new laboratory experiments; continually reviews and refines laboratory material, communicating modifications in a timely manner; assists with developing lab resources for the general chemistry Carmen template courses and the TA Training Forum; assists with determining and maintaining educational technology platforms used for pre- and post-labs; reviews current chemical education and science education research for cutting edge laboratory material; identifies improvements and/or new experiments that better meet course and national professional objectives; cooperates with the general chemistry preparatory lab, along with the other laboratory supervisors and the Undergraduate Program Director, to ensure that the teaching labs are properly equipped and maintained; oversees the contents of laboratory rooms including known and unknown reagents and waste disposal; recommends new equipment for the laboratories; plans and monitors an annual budget for laboratory operation for the entire academic year, autumn, spring, and summer; responds to questions and concerns from students, teaching staff, and instructors related to the teaching laboratories. <br> <br> \r\n\r\nIn cooperation with the Assistant Laboratory Supervisor, answers all laboratory-related emails from students and staff in a timely manner; prepares all academic misconduct cases related to laboratory issues; represents the department in all academic misconduct cases; acts as a role model for exemplary laboratory practice and safety; updates departmental safety videos on a regular basis; assists in the on-going training of general chemistry teaching assistants; develops policies and procedures so that workloads of teaching assistants are distributed evenly and faculty expectations for the teaching assistants are consistent; supervises, reviews and trains laboratory teaching staff and other university employees in appropriate teaching techniques and safe laboratory practices; reviews and evaluates effectiveness of laboratory teaching methods; maintains a pool of student instructional aides and staff teaching associates; helps make decisions regarding hiring, evaluation, promotion, and termination of student instructional aides and staff teaching associates; communicates job expectations to student instructional aides and staff teaching associates; performs monthly payroll certification for all student instructional aides and staff teaching associates for courses supervised; works with faculty and staff to identify quality undergraduate students capable of serving as student instructional aides; determines and monitors the filling of laboratory sections offered each term to ensure optimum staffing, schedules the staffing of all laboratory sections each term, and cooperates with human resources to provide timely hiring decisions of laboratory personnel; cooperates with the instructional staff to provide appropriate assessment instruments for the undergraduate teaching laboratories; writes laboratory related assessment items to connect knowledge and techniques learned in the laboratory to the larger course setting; The Program Manager is responsible for project management of this significant, institute-wide program, which includes a large budget and sizable faculty and staff involvement.  Primary focus areas include partnering with the faculty PI to meet program commitments; communicating effectively with the food, nutrition and pharmaceutical industry, sponsors, stakeholders, and team members; generating, implementing, and managing risk analysis/mitigation and program plans; balancing scope, budget, and schedule; and delivering desired program outcomes.<br>\r\n\r\nThe activities of the Program Manager enable the PI to focus on technical excellence in research.<br><br>\r\n\r\n<b>Performance Objectives</b><br>\r\n1.\tBe responsible to the  Industry Liaison Office and the Personalized Food and Nutritional Metabolomics for Health Director to achieve the full scope of the Foods for Health Discovery Theme objectives<br>\r\n2.\tBalance the competing constraints including scope, quality, schedule, budget, resources, and risk to deliver optimal outcomes<br>\r\n3.\tDefine, frame, and execute a Personalized Food and Nutritional Metabolomics for Health program plan which addresses the needs, concerns, and expectations of internal and external stakeholders as the program is planned and carried out<br>\r\n4.\tIdentify, align, and utilize OSU support functions (ex. Sponsored Programs, Legal Affairs, Technology Commercialization) as required to execute the program plan<br>\r\n5.\tApply knowledge, skills, tools, and techniques to Discovery Theme activities to meet the end deliverable requirements  <br>\r\n6.\tBe responsible for iterative, progressive elaboration of the program plan throughout the program lifecycle, allowing the program team to manage to a greater level of detail and risk control as the program evolves<br>\r\n7.\tEnhance success of the full scope of the program by ensuring that scope, change, planning, product and project quality, timeliness, budget compliance, and degree of customer satisfaction are managed<br><br>\r\n\r\n<b>Performance Competences</b><br>\r\n1.\t[Project Awareness]  Understands OSU organizational structure and political/social landscape.  Advises program team on how the Discovery Theme Initiative and related organizations operate, and provides direction on how to get things done.  Looks at problems from many different perspectives and determines appropriate solutions to program challenges.  Uses knowledge of changing situations and pressures inside OSU and the partner organizations to identify potential organizational problems and opportunities.  Participates in the business strategic planning process for the Personalized Food and Nutritional Metabolomics for Health program.  Identifies critical, high pay-off strategies and prioritizes team efforts accordingly. <br>\r\n2.\t[Effectiveness]  Identifies and develops close, collaborative long-term relationships and agreements between multiple OSU organizations and private sector partners, including food companies, with the intent of accomplishing mutually compatible organizational and program goals that could not be accomplished independently.  Collaborates with business development functions to establish overall strategies and themes that differentiate OSU.  Creates implementation and management plans to monitor and control program cost, schedule, and technical performance.  Develops effective give-and-take relationships with others; understands the agendas and perspectives of others; recognizes and balances the interests and needs of the program with those of the broader organization. <br>\r\n3.\t[Professionalism]  Establishes open, candid, trusting relationships; treats all individuals fairly and with respect; is seen as a direct, truthful individual who can present the unvarnished truth in an appropriate and helpful manner.  Promotes the flow of appropriate information and communication throughout the organization and with partners.  Encourages the open expression of ideas, opinions, and contrary views; listens carefully to input and feedback.  Ensures early and continuous partner participation and communication for clarifying program requirements, assessing implementation progress, and conducting reviews against commitments to achieve the best product value. <br>\r\n4.\t[Communication]  Develops and implements strategic communication plans to support strategic objectives.  Communicates strategically from a broad institutional perspective, clearly and accurately presenting a position while demonstrating an understanding of the needs and sensitivities of varied constituencies. <br>\r\n5.\t[Customer Focus]  Understands partner’s food and nutrition interests and/or business and looks for ways to add value beyond partners’ immediate requests.  Explores, anticipates, and addresses the unidentified, underlying, and long-term partner needs and concerns.  Encourages partners to consider difficult issues that are in their best interests.  Advocates on behalf of partners, identifying approaches that meet their needs as well of those of OSU.  Strategically and systematically evaluates external indicators to project emerging and longer-term opportunities and threats that will impact market needs and program direction. <br>\r\n6.\t[Flexibility]  Adapts behavior, yet maintains focus on objectives amidst continuous change, ambiguity, and turmoil.  Anticipates and capitalizes on emerging opportunities and risks.  Adjusts broad/macro organizational strategies, directions, priorities, structures, and processes to changing needs in the environment.  Adapts interpersonal style to a diverse audience. <br>\r\n7.\t[Innovation]  Creates new concepts, models, approaches, and/or theories that have wide-ranging impacts on the Personalized Food and Nutritional Metabolomics for Health program at Ohio State.  Identifies unique approaches to deal with novel situations for which no known precedent exists.  Creates an enterprise-wide climate that encourages and rewards innovation and receptivity to change.  Anticipates long-term future opportunities and positions OSU to take advantage of them.  Takes risk to drive new initiatives and breakthrough thinking. <br>\r\n8.\t[Teamwork]  Communicates the vision and aligns team goals with strategic objectives.  Builds relationships among new faculty hires, existing faculty, students, food companies and the private sector in general, fosters team spirit and collaboration, and resolves team conflicts.  Breaks down barriers (structural, functional, and cultural) between these stakeholders, facilitating the sharing of expertise and resources that distinguish OSU. The Moritz Law Library’s 700,000 volume equivalents and extensive on-line resources make it the largest law library in Ohio.  The library is an integral part of the vibrant intellectual life of the college.  We seek a librarian who is committed to our high level of customer service and record of excellence.  <br> <br> \r\n\r\nThe principal responsibilities of this position include providing, in a service-oriented environment, sophisticated research and reference assistance to faculty, students and other patrons of the Moritz Law Library, and teaching the required first-year Legal Analysis and Writing I (LAW I) course, which includes legal research, or an advanced legal research course each year, and occasionally lecturing on legal research to classes within the Moritz College of Law and throughout the university.  <br> <br> \r\n\r\nThe Reference Librarian will also take part in the evaluation and selection of information resources, participate in the Moritz Law Library’s faculty and law review liaison programs, work on special projects and serve on Law Library, College of Law and University committees. As a faculty member in the Acquisitions Department, the successful candidate will leverage their expertise in procuring and integrating electronic resources to manage a diverse, multimillion-dollar portfolio of high-impact content within a complex multi-consortia negotiating environment. The Electronic Resources Officer manages the acquisition and maintenance of continuing online resources, including order and renewal of e-journals, e-books, and other online content along with oversight of waning print serial subscriptions. The position will serve as Electronic Resource Officer for OSUL in the Committee on Institutional Cooperation (CIC) and OhioLINK’s Cooperative Information Resources Management Committee.\r\n<br><br>\r\nThe Electronic Resources Officer is responsible for four staff (potentially five) and reports to the Head of Acquisitions. The Librarian works collaboratively with staff in other units focused on collection strategy, information technology, and cataloging to identify, license, and manage ongoing access to electronic resources. This position is a vital contributor to planning, policy-making, and daily operational decision-making within the department. The position will take the lead in liaising with vendors, negotiating licenses, and troubleshooting electronic resources access issues.\r\n<br><br>\r\n\r\nFor complete position description details please visit: http://go.osu.edu/OSUL_Jobs \r\n<br><br>\r\n\r\n\r\n<b>About OSU Libraries:  A Driving Force for Change </b><br>\r\nThe Ohio State University Libraries is a highly valued partner and campus leader in advancing discovery and learning for OSU, for the state of Ohio and for an ever expanding community of world scholars.  Aligned with the University’s vision to be the world’s preeminent public comprehensive university, the Libraries advance student and faculty success by delivering distinctive content and fostering intellectual connections.  \r\n<br><br>\r\n\r\nA world-class public research and comprehensive teaching university such as OSU demands a top research library and OSU Libraries is rising to eminence along with the rest of the University.  The Libraries, a leader among peers, is currently ranked in the top 10 among the public university members of the Association of Research Libraries, a reflection of the investment of the University.  This ranking also places OSU Libraries within the top 20 of 126 ARL member libraries.  The OSU Libraries is an essential charter member of OhioLINK, a consortium of 88 Ohio academic libraries and the State Library of Ohio and shares resources through that organization.  The Libraries also enhances collections and services by participation in the CIC, the academic consortium of Big Ten institutions.  \r\n<br><br>\r\n\r\nWith this support and these partnerships, the OSU Libraries has turned its attention to rapid innovation to address the challenges of the evolving academic environment.  Major renovation projects continue to enhance our spaces for collaborative and dynamic teaching, learning and research.  An ambitious talent management plan is bringing new skills and reframing long held strengths.  Increased investment in a wide variety of digital initiatives aims to revolutionize discovery and access anytime, anywhere to our vast and distinctive resources.  Our impact reaches beyond our campus and extends the land-grant mission internationally. As a faculty member in the Acquisitions Department, the successful candidate will leverage their expertise in procuring and integrating electronic resources to manage a diverse, multimillion-dollar portfolio of high-impact content within a complex multi-consortia negotiating environment. The Electronic Resources Officer manages the acquisition and maintenance of continuing online resources, including order and renewal of e-journals, e-books, and other online content along with oversight of waning print serial subscriptions. The position will serve as Electronic Resource Officer for OSUL in the Committee on Institutional Cooperation (CIC) and OhioLINK’s Cooperative Information Resources Management Committee.\r\n<br><br>\r\nThe Electronic Resources Officer is responsible for four staff (potentially five) and reports to the Head of Acquisitions. The Librarian works collaboratively with staff in other units focused on collection strategy, information technology, and cataloging to identify, license, and manage ongoing access to electronic resources. This position is a vital contributor to planning, policy-making, and daily operational decision-making within the department. The position will take the lead in liaising with vendors, negotiating licenses, and troubleshooting electronic resources access issues.\r\n<br><br>\r\n\r\nFor complete position description details please visit: http://go.osu.edu/OSUL_Jobs \r\n<br><br>\r\n\r\n\r\n<b>About OSU Libraries:  A Driving Force for Change </b><br>\r\nThe Ohio State University Libraries is a highly valued partner and campus leader in advancing discovery and learning for OSU, for the state of Ohio and for an ever expanding community of world scholars.  Aligned with the University’s vision to be the world’s preeminent public comprehensive university, the Libraries advance student and faculty success by delivering distinctive content and fostering intellectual connections.  \r\n<br><br>\r\n\r\nA world-class public research and comprehensive teaching university such as OSU demands a top research library and OSU Libraries is rising to eminence along with the rest of the University.  The Libraries, a leader among peers, is currently ranked in the top 10 among the public university members of the Association of Research Libraries, a reflection of the investment of the University.  This ranking also places OSU Libraries within the top 20 of 126 ARL member libraries.  The OSU Libraries is an essential charter member of OhioLINK, a consortium of 88 Ohio academic libraries and the State Library of Ohio and shares resources through that organization.  The Libraries also enhances collections and services by participation in the CIC, the academic consortium of Big Ten institutions.  \r\n<br><br>\r\n\r\nWith this support and these partnerships, the OSU Libraries has turned its attention to rapid innovation to address the challenges of the evolving academic environment.  Major renovation projects continue to enhance our spaces for collaborative and dynamic teaching, learning and research.  An ambitious talent management plan is bringing new skills and reframing long held strengths.  Increased investment in a wide variety of digital initiatives aims to revolutionize discovery and access anytime, anywhere to our vast and distinctive resources.  Our impact reaches beyond our campus and extends the land-grant mission internationally.
